I be glad to come to the House to discuss this important subject today . the upcoming COP host by the United Arab Emirates be an important moment in the climate crisis . amid record temperature and emission , the first comprehensive stocktake of progress against the Paris agreement at COP28 will show that the world be badly off - track . we have make significant progress through the Paris agreement , with temperature projection shift from 4 ° C before Paris to between 2 . 4 ° C and 2 . 7 ° C after Glasgow through nationally determined contribution commitment , but we know that that be not enough . in Glasgow , we cement the goal of limit global temperature increase to 1 . 5 ° C as our north star . that have be carry forward by the UAE presidency . the late science and the impact we be see , even at 1 . 1 ° C , show we why . a top priority for the United Kingdom be to leave COP28 with a clear road map towards keep 1 . 5 ° C in reach from the global stocktake . the UK head to COP28 with a record at home and internationally that we can be proud of . the Prime Minister recently affirm our commitment to net zero and set out our new approach to get there . at home , we have decarbonise fast than any other major economy — by 48 % since 1990 . look forward , our 2030 target require the large reduction in emission of any major economy . two year on from Glasgow , the need to accelerate action be more urgent than ever . the world need to decarbonise more than five time fast than we have do in the last two decade . at COP28 , we want to see progress against five area : ambitious new commitment and action , include a pathway to keep 1 . 5 ° C within reach from the global stocktake ; scale up clean energy through commitment to triple renewable , double energy efficiency and move beyond fossil fuel ; progress on finance reform , deliver $ 100 billion for develop economy ; build resilience to climate impact , include by double adaptation finance and establish a loss and damage fund ; and , finally , progress on restore nature . action to deliver net zero be not just a matter of do the right thing by avoid harm ; it be crucial to our security and prosperity here in the UK now and in the future . the global net zero transition could be worth £ 1 trillion to UK business between 2021 and 2030 . ( 2 ) in the 2018 Act , after section 40 insert — " 40a process of datum in relation to a case - file prepare by the police service for submission to the Crown Prosecution Service for a charge decision ( 1 ) this section apply to a set of processing operation consist of the preparation of a case - file by the police service for submission to the Crown Prosecution Service for a charge decision , the making of a charge decision by the Crown Prosecution Service , and the return of the case - file by the Crown Prosecution Service to the police service after a charging decision have be make . ( 2 ) the police service be not oblige to comply with the first data protection principle except insofar as that principle require process to be fair , or the third datum protection principle , in prepare a case - file for submission to the Crown Prosecution Service for a charge decision . ( 3 ) the Crown Prosecution Service be not oblige to comply with the first data protection principle except insofar as that principle require process to be fair , or the third datum protection principle , in make a charge decision on a case - file submit for that purpose by the police service . ( 4 ) if the Crown Prosecution Service decide that a charge will not be pursue when it make a charge decision on a case - file submit for that purpose by the police service it must take all step reasonably require to destroy and delete all copy of the case - file in its possession . ( 5 ) if the Crown Prosecution Service decide that a charge will be pursue when it make a charge decision on a case - file submit for that purpose by the police service it must return the case - file to the police service and take all step reasonably require to destroy and delete all copy of the case - file in its possession . ( 6 ) where the Crown Prosecution Service decide that a charge will be pursue when it make a charge decision on a case - file submit for that purpose by the police service and return the case - file to the police service under subsection ( 5 ) , the police service must comply with the first data protection principle and the third data protection principle in relation to any subsequent processing of the datum contain in the case - file . " this include any record information that be connect with any log or audit associate with an Identity Assurance Service . " General Data . " this mean any other record information which be not personal datum , audit datum or relationship datum , but be still connect with a " Service User " . " Personal Data . " this take its meaning from the Data Protection Act 2018 or subsequent legislation ( e . g . any recorded information that relate to a " Service User " who be also an identified or identifiable live individual ) . " Relationship Data . " this mean any record information that describe ( or infer ) a relationship between a " Service User " , " Identity Provider " or " Service Provider " with another " Service User " , " Identity Provider " or " Service Provider " and include any cookie or program whose purpose be to supply a means through which relationship datum be collect . 3 other term use in relation to the Principles be define as follow — " save - line2Identity Assurance Service . " this include relevant application of the technology ( e . g . hardware , software , database , documentation ) in the possession or control of any " Service User " , " Identity Provider " or " Service Provider " that be use to facilitate identity assurance activity ; it also include any ida datum process by that technology or by an Identity Provider or by a Service Provider in the context of the Service ; and any ida Data process by the underlie infrastructure for the purpose of deliver the ida service or associate billing , management , audit and fraud prevention . " Identity Provider . " this mean the certify individual or certify organisation that provide an Identity Assurance Service ( e . g . establish an identity , verification of identity ) ; it include any agent of a certify Identity Provider that process ida datum in connection with that Identity Assurance Service . " Participant . " this mean any " Identity Provider " , " Service Provider " or " Service User " in an Identity Assurance Service . a " Participant " include any agent by definition . " process . " in the context of ida datum mean " collect , use , disclose , retain , transmit , copy , compare , corroborate , correlate , aggregate , access " the datum and include any other operation perform on ida datum . " Provider . " include both " Identity Provider " and / or " Service Provider " . " Service Provider . " this mean the certify individual or certify organisation that provide a service that use an Identity Provider in order to verify identity of the Service User ; it include any agent of the Service Provider that process ida datum from an Identity Assurance Service . " Service User . " this mean the person ( I . e . an organisation ( incorporate or not ) ) or an individual ( dead or alive ) who have establish ( or be establish ) an identity with an Identity Provider ; it include an agent ( e . g . a solicitor , family member ) who act on behalf of a Service User with proper authority ( e . g . a public guardian , or a Director of a company , or someone who possess power of attorney ) . the person may be live or decease ( the identity may still need to be use once its owner be dead , for example by an executor ) . " Third Party . " this mean any person ( I . e . any organisation or individual ) who be not a " Participant " ( e . g . the police or a regulator ) . part 2 - the Nine Identity Assurance principle any exemption from these principle must be specify via the " Exceptional Circumstances Principle " . ( see Principle 9 ) . 1 User Control Principle Statement of Principle : " I can exercise control over identity assurance activity affect I and these can only take place if I consent or approve they . " 1 . 1 an Identity Provider or Service Provider must ensure any collection , use or disclosure of ida datum in , or from , an Identity Assurance Service be approve by each particular Service User who be connect with the ida datum . 1 . 2 there should be no compulsion to use the Identity Assurance Service and Service Providers should offer alternative mechanism to access their service . fail to do so would undermine the consensual nature of the service . 2 Transparency Principle Statement of Principle : " identity assurance can only take place in way I understand and when I be fully inform . " 2 . 1 each Identity Provider or Service Provider must be able to justify to Service Users why their ida datum be process . ensure transparency of activity and effective oversight through auditing and other activity inspire public trust and confidence in how their detail be use . 2 . 2 each Service User must be offer a clear description about the processing of ida datum in advance of any processing . Identity Providers must be transparent with user about their particular model for service provision . 2 . 3 the information provide include a clear explanation of why any specific information have to be provide by the Service User ( e . g . in order that a particular level of identity assurance can be obtain ) and identify any obligation on the part of the Service User ( e . g . in relation to the User ' s role in secure his / her own identity information ) . 2 . 4 the Service User will be able to identify which Service Provider they be use at any give time . 2 . 5 any subsequent and significant change to the processing arrangement that have be previously describe to a Service User require the prior consent or approval of that Service User before it come into effect . 2 . 6 all procedure , include those involve with security , should be make publicly available at the appropriate time , unless such transparency present a security or privacy risk . for example , the standard of encryption can be identify without jeopardy to the encryption key be use . 3 Multiplicity Principle Statement of Principle : " I can use and choose as many different identifier or identity provider as I want to . " 3 . 1 a Service User be free to use any number of identifier that each uniquely identify the individual or business concern . 3 . 2 a Service User can use any of his identity establish with an Identity Provider with any Service Provider . 3 . 3 a Service User shall not be oblige to use any Identity Provider or Service Provider not choose by that Service User ; however , a Service Provider can require the Service User to provide a specific level of Identity Assurance , appropriate to the Service User ' s request to a Service Provider . 3 . 4 a Service User can choose any number of Identity Providers and where possible can choose between Service Providers in order to meet his or her diverse need . where a Service User choose to register with more than one Identity Provider , Identity Providers and Service Providers must not link the Service User ' s different account or gain information about their use of other Providers . 3 . 5 a Service User can terminate , suspend or change Identity Provider and where possible can choose between Service Providers at any time . 3 . 6 a Service Provider do not know the identity of the Identity Provider use by a Service User to verify an identity in relation to a specific service . the Service Provider know that the Identity Provider can be trust because the Identity Provider have be certify , as set out in GPG43 – Requirements for Secure Delivery of Online Public Services ( rsdops ) . 4 Data Minimisation Principle Statement of Principle : " my interaction only use the minimum datum necessary to meet my need . " 4 . 1 Identity Assurance should only be use where a need have be establish and only to the appropriate minimum level of assurance . 4 . 2 Identity Assurance datum process by an Identity Provider or a Service Provider to facilitate a request of a Service User must be the minimum necessary in order to fulfil that request in a secure and auditable manner . 4 . 3 when a Service User stop use a particular Identity Provider , their datum should be delete . datum should be retain only where require for specific target fraud , security or other criminal investigation purpose . 5 Data Quality Principle Statement of Principle : " my interaction only use the minimum datum necessary to meet my need . " 5 . 1 Service Providers should enable Service Users ( or authorise person , such as the holder of a Power of Attorney ) to be able to update their own personal datum , at a time at their choosing , free of charge and in a simple and easy manner . 5 . 2 Identity Providers and Service Providers must take account of the appropriate level of identity assurance require before allow any updating of personal datum . 6 Service User Access and Portability Principle Statement of Principle : " I have to be provide with copy of all of my datum on request ; I can move / remove my datum whenever I want . " 6 . 1 each Identity Provider or Service Provider must allow , promptly , on request and free of charge , each Service User access to any ida datum that relate to that Service User . 6 . 2 it shall be unlawful to make it a condition of do anything in relation to a Service User to request or require that Service User to request ida datum . 6 . 3 the Service User must be able to require an Identity Provider to transfer his personal datum , to a second Identity Provider in a standard electronic format , free of charge and without impediment or delay . 7 Certification Principle Statement of Principle : " I can have confidence in the Identity Assurance Service because all the participant have to be certify against common governance requirement . " 7 . 1 as a baseline control , all Identity Providers and Service Providers will be certify against a share standard . this be one important way of build trust and confidence in the service . 7 . 2 as part of the certification process , Identity Providers and Service Providers be oblige to co - operate with the independent Third Party and accept their impartial determination and to ensure that contractual arrangement — • reinforce the application of the Identity Assurance Principles • contain a reference to the independent Third Party as a mechanism for dispute resolution . 7 . 3 in the context of personal datum , certification procedure include the use of Privacy Impact Assessments , Security risk assessment , Privacy by Design concept and , in the context of information security , a commitment to use appropriate technical measure ( e . g . encryption ) and ever improve security management . wherever possible , such certification process and security procedure reliant on technical device should be make publicly available at the appropriate time . 7 . 4 all Identity Providers and Service Providers will take all reasonable step to ensure that a Third Party can not capture ida datum that confirm ( or infer ) the existence of relationship between any Participant . no relationship between party or record should be establish without the consent of the Service User . 7 . 5 Certification can be revoke if there be significant non - compliance with any Identity Assurance Principle . 8 Dispute Resolution Principle Statement of Principle : " if I have a dispute , I can go to an independent Third Party for a resolution . " 8 . 1 a Service User who , after a reasonable time , can not , or be unable , to resolve a complaint or problem directly with an Identity Provider or Service Provider can call upon an independent Third Party to seek resolution of the issue . this could happen for example where there be a disagreement between the Service User and the Identity Provider about the accuracy of datum . 8 . 2 the independent Third Party can resolve the same or similar complaint affect a group of Service Users . 8 . 3 the independent Third Party can co - operate with other regulator in order to resolve problem and can raise relevant issue of importance concern the Identity Assurance Service . 8 . 4 an adjudication / recommendation of the independent Third Party should be publish . the independent Third Party must operate transparently , but detailed case history should only be publish subject to appropriate review and consent . 8 . 5 there can be more than one independent Third Party . 8 . 6 the independent Third Party can recommend change to standard or certification procedure or that an Identity Provider or Service Provider should lose their certification . 9 Exceptional Circumstances Principle Statement of Principle : " any exception have to be approve by Parliament and be subject to independent scrutiny . " 9 . 1 any exemption from the application of any of the above Principles to ida datum shall only be lawful if it be link to a statutory framework that legitimise all Identity Assurance Services , or an Identity Assurance Service in the context of a specific service . in the absence of such a legal framework then alternative measure must be take to ensure , transparency , scrutiny and accountability for any exception . 9 . 2 any exemption from the application of any of the above Principles that relate to the processing of personal datum must also be necessary and justifiable in term of one of the criterion in Article 8 ( 2 ) of the European Convention of Human Rights : namely in the interest of national security ; public safety or the economic well - being of the country ; for the prevention of disorder or crime ; for the protection of health or moral , or for the protection of the right and freedom of other . 9 . 3 any subsequent processing of personal datum by any Third Party who have obtain such datum in exceptional circumstance ( as identify by Article 8 ( 2 ) above ) must be the minimum necessary to achieve that ( or another ) exceptional circumstance . 9 . 4 any exceptional circumstance involve the processing of personal datum must be subject to a Privacy Impact Assessment by all relevant " data controller " ( where " datum controller " take its meaning from the Data Protection Act ) . 9 . 5 any exemption from the application of any of the above Principles in relation to ida datum shall remain subject to the Dispute Resolution Principle . I rise to speak to new clause 1 in my name and that of other colleague . early this year , I meet with member of Leicestershire Police Federation , who raise concern about element of the Data Protection Act 2018 that be impose unnecessary and burdensome redaction obligation on police force . I thank the national Police Federation for its tireless campaign on this issue , particularly Ben Hudson of Suffolk police , and I thank my hon . friend the Member for Waveney ( Peter Aldous ) for all he have do in this area . I thank they for much of the information I will share today . as I explain in Committee , part 3 of the 2018 Act implement the law enforcement directive and make provision for datum processing by competent authority , include police force and the Crown Prosecution Service , for law enforcement purpose . paragraph ( 4 ) of the enforcement directive emphasise that the " free flow of personal datum between competent authority for the purpose of the prevention , investigation , detection or prosecution of criminal offence … should be facilitate while ensure a high level of protection of personal datum . " however , part 3 of the 2018 Act contain no provision at all to facilitate the free flow of personal datum between the police and the CPS . instead , it impose burdensome obligation on the police , require they to redact personal datum from information transfer to the CPS . those obligation be only delay and obstruct the expeditious progress of the criminal justice system and be not even mandate by the law enforcement directive . the problem have arise due to chapter 2 of part 3 of the 2018 Act , which set out six datum protection principle that apply to data processing by competent authority for law enforcement purpose . section 35 ( 1 ) state : " the first data protection principle be that the processing of personal datum for any of the law enforcement purpose must be lawful and fair . " section 35 ( 2 ) state : " the processing of personal datum for any of the law enforcement purpose be lawful only if and to the extent that it be base on law and either — ( a ) the data subject have give consent to the processing for that purpose , or ( b ) the processing be necessary for the performance of a task carry out for that purpose by a competent authority . the Police Federation have say that it be unlikely that section 35 ( 2 ) ( a ) will apply in this context . it have also say that in the case of 35 ( 2 ) ( b ) , the test of whether the processing be " necessary " be exact , require a competent authority to apply its mind to the proportionality of process specific item of personal datum for the particular law enforcement purpose in question . under section 35 ( 3 ) to 35 ( 5 ) , where the processing be " sensitive processing " , an even more rigorous test apply , require among other thing that the processing be " strictly necessary for the law enforcement purpose " in question . section 37 state : " the third data protection principle be that personal datum process for any of the law enforcement purpose must be adequate , relevant and not excessive in relation to the purpose for which it be process . " for the purpose of the 2018 Act , the Crown Prosecution Service and each police force be separate competent authority and separate datum controller . therefore , as set out in section 34 ( 3 ) , the CPS and each police force must comply with the data protection principle . a transfer of information by a police force to the CPS amount to the processing of personal datum . the test of " necessary " and " strictly necessary " under the first and third datum protection principle require a competent authority to identify and consider each and every item of personal datum contain within the information that it be intend to process and to consider whether it be necessary for that item of personal datum to be process in the manner intend . the impact of this be that when prepare a case file for a charge decision from the CPS , the police must spend huge amount of time and resource analyse information that have be gather by investigate officer in order to identify every item of personal datum . they then have to decide whether it be necessary or , in many case strictly necessary , for the CPS to consider each item of personal datum when make its charge decision , and to redact every item of personal datum that do not meet that test . the National Police Chiefs ' Council and the CPS have produce detailed guidance on this redaction process . it emphasise that the 2018 Act be a legal requirement and that the police and the CPS do not have any special relationship that negate the need to redact and protect personal information . the combination of the requirement of the guidance and of the Act represent a huge amount of administrative work for police officer , result in hour of prepare appropriate redaction . furthermore , such work be inevitably carry out by relatively junior officer who have no particular expertise in data protection , and much of it may never be use by the CPS if the matter be not charge or if the defendant plead guilty before trial . nationally , about 25 % of case that be submit to the CPS be not charge . a significant proportion of that time and money could be save if the redaction of personal datum by the police occur after , rather than before , a charge decision have be make by the CPS . the burden that this be place on police force be highlight in the 2022 " Annual Review of Disclosure " by the Attorney General ' s Office , which hear evidence from police that " redaction of material for disclosure be place a significant pressure on resource " . it also find that one police force have invest £ 1 million in a disclosure specialist team solely to deal with redaction . in its report on police priority , the Home Affairs Committee state : " the National Police Chiefs ' Council and the College of Policing say this ' labour - intensive ' process ' tie up police resource for a protect period of time ' , mean investigation take long , and possibly add to the likelihood of victim withdraw their support for a case . the College note that the problem have become bad as digital device such as phone and laptop have develop ever great storage capacity , mean there be more datum for the police to process and redact . disparity in digital capability across the 43 local force also exacerbate the problem . " the report go on to say : " lengthy and inefficient redaction process and protract investigation be neither effective nor fair on either victim or suspect . the handling of case file need to comply with data protection law . however , ensure that the requirement be proportionate and that force have the digital capacity to meet such requirement efficiently be an urgent issue that need address . More need to be do to pilot solution and get the balance right . " furthermore , the Police Federation and the National Police Chiefs ' Council estimate that the cost nationally of the redaction exercise be over £ 5 . 6 million per annum . there be no disputing that there be a clear issue here , and I welcome that this have be acknowledge by Ministers I have be engage with , include the Minister for Crime , Policing and Fire , my right hon . friend the Member for Croydon South ( Chris Philp ) ; the former Home Secretary , my right hon . and learn Friend the Member for Fareham ( Suella Braverman ) ; and the Minister for Data and Digital Infrastructure , the right hon . member for Maldon ( Sir John Whittingdale ) . only last week , the latter emphasise to I the Government ' s support for reform . indeed , the autumn statement last week highlight the Government ' s commitment to boost public sector productivity by run an ambitious public sector productivity programme with all Departments to reimagine the way public service be deliver . the focus of that will be on " reduce the amount of time our key frontline worker , include police , doctor , and nurse , spend on administrative task " . that be to ensure that they can spend more time deliver for the public . arguably , the current process of datum redaction be the big unnecessary administrative task keep police officer away from the frontline , so reform need to be implement urgently . my new clause lay out a blueprint for that reform and would insert a propose new section into the 2018 Act to exempt the police service and the CPS from comply with the first data protection principle — except in so far as that principle require process to be fair — or with the third data protection principle when prepare a case file for submission to the CPS for a charge decision , thereby facilitate the free flow of personal datum between the police and the CPS . if the CPS decide to charge , the case file would be return to the police to carry out the redaction exercise before there be any risk of the file be disclose to any person or body other than the CPS . in the 25 % of case in which the CPS decide not to charge , the unredacted file would simply be delete by the CPS . my new clause would have no obvious disadvantage , as the security of the personal datum would not be compromise and the necessary redaction would still be undertake once a charging decision have be make . furthermore , provide material unredacted to the CPS pre - charge would not impact the timeliness of the process in any way , as the police would still be provide the same material to the CPS as they would have do previously , just unredacted . I know from my conversation with Ministers that there be a few question from a number of source about whether legislative change be the good way to tackle the issue surround redaction . to that , the Police Federation have say that " the hope be that the CPS will set out , within their charge advice , what material they intend to rely upon and , therefore , only the require material will have to be redact by the police . this would be do in line with the maximum time of service set out within the ' well case management handbook Jan 23 ' , which state that service be require no less than five day before the hearing . so we must accept that there may be a slight delay in the CPS be able to serve their case on the defence at the point of charge . but the time in which it will take police force to apply for a charge decision to the CPS will be far quick without the need for redact . thus , stop defendant be on bail or under ' release under investigation ' status for as long as they currently be and victim of crime wait less time for charge decision . " in addition , the Police Federation have highlight that while auto - redaction software will help to mitigate the current issue , it will not recover all policing capacity in respect of redaction . officer will still need to review the item to consider what auto - redaction parameter need apply , otherwise police could risk end up with mass over - redaction , and have to check to ensure nothing have be miss . the real benefit for auto - redaction software will come post - charge , especially if the CPS state exactly what material it intend to use or disclose . I also appreciate that the Government feel they can not support my amendment because of three technical legal point , and I would like to summarise the Police Federation ' s response to this , base on advice from its lead counsel who be experience in the field of datum protection and privacy . the Government ' s first objection be that there be provision in the 2018 Act , other than the first and third data protection principle , that " in effect require the material concern to be review and redact " . the two example give by the Home Office be the sixth datum protection principle and section 44 . the sixth data protection principle — datum security — do not require case file to be redact . the same standard of " appropriate technical or organisational measure " be require whether case file be redact before or after the CPS have make a charge decision . the Police Federation ' s lead counsel have point out that section 44 ( 4 ) of the Act already contain potentially relevant restriction on a data subject ' s right . those restriction during an investigation would be consistent with an amendment provide for the police to redact any give case file only after the CPS have decide to charge . on the Home Office ' s second objection , that a broad amendment " may be problematic for the ICO and international stakeholder " , the legal expert have highlight that the propose new clause seek only to determine the respective responsibility of the police and the CPS in the processing involve in prepare and submit a case file to the CPS for a charge decision . it would not remove any substantive protection or the obligation to review and redact the personal datum in case file material . it simply provide for such review and redaction by the police after — rather than before — a charge decision have be make . the law enforcement directive , on which the relevant part of the 2018 Act be base , would have permit that when the Act be pass , and I be tell there be no legal reason why it can not be introduce now . on the Home Office ' s third objection , that other privacy law might require the police to review and redact case file even if the 2018 Act be amend in the manner suggest by the Police Federation , the legal expert have point out that datum protection legislation do not generally seek to regulate other privacy - protect law . the impact of the Act on journalism be a good example , as the journalism exemption in part 5 of schedule 2 do not seek to regulate the common - law tort of misuse of private information . data protection legislation should be appropriately calibrate in a particular area even if other legal rule may also have a role in that area . at present , the data protection obligation give rise to the problem . the legal expert believe that it be mere speculation whether other legal rule might give rise to a similar problem if those obligation be amend . it be crucial that we do everything possible to ease the administrative burden on police officer , to free up thousand of police hour and get police back on to the frontline , support community and tackle crime . my new clause would go a long way to achieve that , by facilitate the free flow of personal datum between the police and the CPS , which would speed up the criminal justice process and reduce the burden on the taxpayer — a stated aim of the Government . how disheartening it must be for a police officer to take time and patience redact datum only to find that the case do not go forward , as occur in 25 % of case . common sense must prevail . New Clause 48 - processing of personal datum reveal political opinion " ( 1 ) schedule 1 to the Data Protection Act 2018 ( special category of personal datum ) be amend in accordance with subsection ( 2 ) to ( 5 ) . ( 2 ) after paragraph 21 insert — ' democratic engagement 21a ( 1 ) this condition be meet where — ( a ) the personal datum process be personal datum reveal political opinion , ( b ) the data subject be age 14 or over , and ( c ) the processing fall within sub - paragraph ( 2 ) , subject to the exception in sub - paragraph ( 3 ) and ( 4 ) . ( 2 ) processing fall within this sub - paragraph if — ( a ) the processing — ( i ) be carry out by an elect representative or a person act with the authority of such a representative , and ( ii ) be necessary for the purpose of discharge the elect representative ' s function or for the purpose of the elect representative ' s democratic engagement activity , ( b ) the processing — ( i ) be carry out by a register political party , and ( ii ) be necessary for the purpose of the party ' s election activity or democratic engagement activity , ( c ) the processing — ( i ) be carry out by a candidate for election as an elect representative or a person act with the authority of such a candidate , and ( ii ) be necessary for the purpose of the candidate ' s campaign for election , ( d ) the processing — ( i ) be carry out by a permit participant in relation to a referendum or a person act with the authority of such a person , and ( ii ) be necessary for the purpose of the permit participant ' s campaign in connection with the referendum , or ( e ) the processing — ( i ) be carry out by an accredited campaigner in relation to a recall petition or a person act with the authority of such a person , and ( ii ) be necessary for the purpose of the accredited campaigner ' s campaign in connection with the recall petition . ( 3 ) processing do not meet the condition in sub - paragraph ( 1 ) if it be likely to cause substantial damage or substantial distress to an individual . ( 4 ) processing do not meet the condition in sub - paragraph ( 1 ) if — ( a ) an individual who be the data subject ( or one of the data subject ) have give notice in write to the controller require the controller not to process personal datum in respect of which the individual be the data subject ( and have not give notice in writing withdraw that requirement ) , ( b ) the notice give the controller a reasonable period in which to stop process such datum , and ( c ) that period have end . ( 5 ) for the purpose of sub - paragraph ( 2 ) ( a ) and ( b ) — ( a ) " democratic engagement activity " mean activity whose purpose be to support or promote democratic engagement ; ( b ) " democratic engagement " mean engagement by the public , a section of the public or a particular person with , or with an aspect of , an electoral system or other democratic process in the United Kingdom , either generally or in connection with a particular matter , whether by participate in the system or process or engage with it in another way ; ( c ) example of democratic engagement activity include activity whose purpose be — ( i ) to promote the registration of individual as elector ; ( ii ) to increase the number of elector participate in election for elect representative , referendum or process for recall petition in which they be entitle to participate ; ( iii ) to support an elect representative or register political party in discharge function , or carry on other activity , describe in sub - paragraph ( 2 ) ( a ) or ( b ) ; ( iv ) to support a person to become a candidate for election as an elect representative ; ( v ) to support a campaign or campaigning refer to in sub - paragraph ( 2 ) ( c ) , ( d ) or ( e ) ; ( vi ) to raise fund to support activity whose purpose be describe in sub - paragraph ( i ) to ( v ) ; ( d ) example of activity that may be democratic engagement activity include — ( i ) gather opinion , whether by carry out a survey or by other mean ; ( ii ) communicate with elector . code of practice : approval by the Secretary of State Amendment make : 45 , page 56 , line 23 , leave out subsection ( 2 ) and insert — " ( 2 ) after section 124C ( insert by section 32 of this Act ) insert — 124D Secretary of State ' s recommendation ( 1 ) where a code be prepare under section 121 , 122 , 123 , 124 or 124a , the Commissioner must — ( a ) submit what the Commissioner consider to be the final version to the Secretary of State , and ( b ) publish it . ( 2 ) before the end of the period of 40 day begin when the code be submit to the Secretary of State , the Secretary of State must — ( a ) decide whether to make recommendation relate to the code ( whether about its content or about other matter ) , ( b ) send any recommendation to the Commissioner in writing , and ( c ) publish the recommendation . ( 3 ) if the Secretary of State do not make recommendation , the Secretary of State must lay the code before Parliament . ( 4 ) if the Secretary of State make recommendation , the Commissioner must , before the end of the response period — ( a ) consider the recommendation , ( b ) decide whether to withdraw the code , and ( c ) prepare and publish a document respond to the recommendation . ( 5 ) in subsection ( 4 ) , " the response period " mean — ( a ) the period of 40 day begin when the recommendation be publish , or ( b ) such long period as the Secretary of State and the Commissioner may agree . ( 6 ) the document respond to the recommendation must — ( a ) state whether the Commissioner accept each recommendation , ( b ) give reason for accept , or not accept , each recommendation , ( c ) state the step that the Commissioner have take , or propose to take , in response to each recommendation , ( d ) state whether the code be withdraw , and ( e ) where relevant , give reason for not withdraw the code . ( 7 ) if the document state that the code be not withdraw , the Secretary of State must lay the code before Parliament . ( 2 ) the power may be exercise only for the purpose of assist the Secretary of State in identify case which merit further consideration to establish whether relevant benefit be be pay or have be pay in accordance with the enactment and rule of law relate to those benefit . account information notice 2 ( 1 ) an account information notice be a notice require a person to give the Secretary of State — ( a ) the name of the holder of account that the person identify as be match account in relation to a specified relevant benefit , ( b ) other specify information relate to the holder of those account , and ( c ) such further information in connection with those account as may be specify . ( 2 ) an account information notice — ( a ) may require information relate to a person who hold a matching account even if the person do not claim a relevant benefit ; ( b ) may not require information relate to any person who do not hold a matching account . ( 3 ) " matching account " , in relation to a specified relevant benefit , be account — ( a ) link to the receipt of that benefit , and ( b ) in relation to which specify criterion relevant to that benefit , or specify criterion include such criterion , be meet ( for example , criterion about account balance or transaction outside the United Kingdom ) . ( 4 ) depend on the provision make by an account information notice , an account link to the receipt of a relevant benefit may be a matching account if specify criterion be meet in relation to a combination of account that include that account . ( 5 ) an account be to be regard as link to the receipt of a particular relevant benefit if it be — ( a ) an account into which the benefit be ( or be to be ) pay , ( b ) an account into which the benefit have be pay , or ( c ) an account link to an account within paragraph ( a ) or ( b ) . ( 6 ) an account be to be regard as link to another if the same person hold both account . ( 7 ) an account information notice may not be frame in such a way as to require a person to interrogate historic datum . ( 8 ) Data be historic , in relation to a day when a person carry out a process to identify matching account , if it relate to a time before the beginning of the period of one year end with that day . ( 9 ) information provide to the Secretary of State on a particular day in response to an account information notice must relate to account identify by mean of a process carry out no more than seven day before that day . ( 10 ) in this paragraph and paragraph 3 " specified " mean — ( a ) in the case of a relevant benefit , specify or denote by a code in an account information notice ; ( b ) in every other case , specify or describe in an account information notice . further provision about account information notice 3 ( 1 ) an account information notice may require the provision of document , include the provision of a legible and intelligible copy of information record otherwise than in a legible form , and reference in this schedule to the provision of information be to be read accordingly . ( 2 ) an account information notice may require information to be provide at specify interval for a period not exceed one year from the date of the notice . ( 3 ) an account information notice other than one within sub - paragraph ( 2 ) must state the date by which or the period within which the information must be provide . ( 4 ) an account information notice must give detail about — ( a ) right of appeal , and ( b ) the consequence of not comply with the notice . ( 5 ) an account information notice may require information — ( a ) to be compile or collate in a specified manner ; ( b ) to be provide in a specify way ( include by electronic transmission to a specified address or portal ) . ( 6 ) the Secretary of State may vary or cancel an account information notice by notice to the person to whom it be give . restriction on processing and data protection ( 1 ) except as provide by sub - paragraph ( 2 ) , processing of information carry out in compliance with an account information notice do not breach — ( a ) any obligation of confidence owe by the person process the information , or ( b ) any other restriction on the processing of information ( however impose ) . ( 2 ) the power confer by paragraph 1 do not authorise , and be not exercisable to require — ( a ) processing of personal datum that would contravene the data protection legislation ( but in determine whether processing of personal datum would do so , that power be to be take into account ) ; ( b ) processing of information that be prohibit by any of Parts 1 to 7 or chapter 1 of Part 9 of the Investigatory Powers Act 2016 . use of information 5 ( 1 ) information provide to the Secretary of State in response to an account information notice may be use by the Secretary of State only for the purpose of , or for any purpose connect with , the exercise of departmental function . ( 2 ) " departmental function " have the same meaning as in section 127 of the Welfare Reform Act 2012 . part 2 - Code of practice Code of practice 6 ( 1 ) the Secretary of State may issue a code of practice in connection with account information notice . ( 3 ) if the Secretary of State decide to issue a code of practice , the Secretary of State must first prepare and publish a draft of the code of practice . ( 4 ) if the Secretary of State consider it appropriate to proceed after consider any representation make concern the draft and make any change that the Secretary of State consider appropriate , the Secretary of State must — ( a ) issue the code of practice , and ( b ) lie it before Parliament . ( 5 ) the code of practice come into force on the day on which it be issue . code of practice : revision 7 ( 1 ) the Secretary of State may from time to time revise and re - issue the code of practice . ( 2 ) sub - paragraph ( 3 ) to ( 5 ) of paragraph 6 apply in relation to a re - issue of the code of practice as they apply in relation to the first code of practice . ( 3 ) but sub - paragraph ( 3 ) and ( 4 ) of paragraph 6 do not apply if the only change to be make to the code of practice be — ( a ) update of reference to legislation or document which have become out of date , or ( b ) other minor correction . ( 4 ) the Secretary of State may withdraw a code of practice . code of practice : further provision 8 ( 1 ) the Secretary of State must have regard to a code of practice that be for the time be in force under this Part in exercise , or decide whether to exercise , any function to which the code of practice be relevant . ( 2 ) a person ' s failure to observe any provision of a code of practice do not of itself make the person liable to any legal proceeding . ( 3 ) a code of practice be admissible in evidence in any legal proceeding . part 3 - penalty Penalties for failure to comply 9 ( 1 ) if the Secretary of State consider that a person who have be give an account information notice have fail to comply with it , the Secretary of State must give the person an opportunity to make representation about the failure . ( 2 ) sub - paragraph ( 3 ) apply if , have consider any representation that be make , the Secretary of State have reasonable ground to believe that the person have fail to comply with the account information notice and have no reasonable excuse for the failure . ( 3 ) the Secretary of State may give the person — ( a ) a notice require the person to pay a penalty of a prescribed amount ( a " fix penalty " ) ; ( b ) a notice require the person to pay a penalty calculate by reference to a daily rate ( a " daily rate penalty " ) ; ( c ) a notice require the person to pay a fix penalty and a daily rate penalty . ( 4 ) a notice under sub - paragraph ( 3 ) be refer to in this schedule as a penalty notice . ( 5 ) a penalty notice impose a fix penalty must state — ( a ) the amount of the penalty , and ( b ) the period within which it must be pay . ( 6 ) a penalty notice impose a daily rate penalty must — ( a ) state the daily rate of the penalty , ( b ) state the date from which the penalty will begin to be payable , which must not be early than the day after the last date on which an appeal against the penalty may be bring under paragraph 14 , and ( c ) state that the penalty will continue to be payable at the daily rate until the date on which the person comply with the account information notice or such early date as may be specify . ( 7 ) a penalty notice must also include information as to — ( a ) the failure to which the penalty relate , ( b ) how payment may be make , ( c ) right of appeal , and ( d ) the consequence of non - payment ( include , in the case of a daily rate penalty , the potential for the penalty to be increase as describe in paragraph 10 ) . ( 8 ) the Secretary of State may vary or cancel a penalty notice by notice to the person to whom it be give . ( 9 ) the maximum amount of a fix penalty that may be prescribe be £ 1 , 000 . ( 10 ) subject to paragraph 10 , the daily rate of a daily rate penalty be to be such rate as the Secretary of State consider appropriate but it must not exceed £ 40 . increase daily rate penalty 10 ( 1 ) this paragraph apply if — ( a ) a daily rate penalty be impose on a person by a penalty notice , and ( b ) the failure to which the penalty relate continue for more than 30 day begin with the first date on which the daily rate penalty be payable . ( 2 ) the Secretary of State may make an application to the Tribunal for an increase daily rate penalty to be payable by the person . ( 3 ) the Tribunal may determine that an increase daily rate penalty should be payable , and in that case , must determine the increase daily rate and the date from which the increase penalty will begin to be payable . ( 4 ) in decide the increase daily rate , the Tribunal must , in particular , have regard to — ( a ) the likely cost to the person of not comply with the account information notice , ( b ) any benefit to the person of not comply with it , and ( c ) any benefit to anyone else result from the person ' s non - compliance . ( 5 ) the Tribunal may not determine a daily rate that exceed £ 1 , 000 . ( 6 ) the Secretary of State must notify the person of the Tribunal ' s determination . recovery of penalty 11 ( 1 ) in England and Wales , a penalty be recoverable — ( a ) if the county court so order , as if it be payable under an order of that court ; ( b ) if the High Court so order , as if it be payable under an order of that court . ( 2 ) in Scotland , a penalty may be enforce in the same manner as an extract register decree arbitral bear a warrant for execution issue by the sheriff court of any sheriffdom in Scotland . ( 3 ) in this paragraph " penalty " mean a penalty impose by a penalty notice . power to change maximum amount of penalty 12 Regulations may amend the amount for the time be specify in paragraph 9 ( 9 ) or ( 10 ) or 10 ( 5 ) to reflect a change in the value of money . part 4 - Appeals Appeals against account information notice 13 ( 1 ) a person who be give an account information notice may appeal to the Tribunal against the notice , or any requirement of it , on any of the follow ground — ( a ) the person be not a person to whom a notice may be give , ( b ) a requirement of the notice be inconsistent with provision make by paragraph 2 , or ( c ) it be unduly onerous to comply with the notice or requirement . ( 2 ) notice of an appeal under sub - paragraph ( 1 ) must be give before the end of the period of 30 day begin with the date on which the account information notice be give . ( 3 ) on an appeal under sub - paragraph ( 1 ) , the Tribunal may confirm , vary or quash the account information notice or a requirement of it , include by vary the period within which , or the frequency with which , information be to be provide . ( 4 ) if an appeal be bring against an account information notice or any requirement of it , the notice or requirement ( as the case may be ) be of no effect until the appeal be determine or withdraw , unless the Tribunal order otherwise . appeal against penalty notice 14 ( 1 ) a person who be give a penalty notice may appeal to the Tribunal against — ( a ) the notice , ( b ) the amount of the penalty , or ( c ) in the case of a daily rate penalty , the period during which the daily amount be payable . ( 2 ) but sub - paragraph ( 1 ) ( b ) do not give a right of appeal against the amount of an increase daily rate penalty determine by the Tribunal under paragraph 10 . ( 3 ) notice of an appeal under sub - paragraph ( 1 ) must be give before the end of the period of 30 day begin with the date on which the penalty notice be give . ( 4 ) on an appeal under sub - paragraph ( 1 ) , the Tribunal may — ( a ) confirm or quash the decision to impose the penalty , ( b ) confirm or vary the amount of the penalty , ( c ) confirm or vary the period within which all or part of the penalty be to be pay . ( 5 ) if an appeal be bring under sub - paragraph ( 1 ) , the penalty which be the subject of the appeal be not payable until the appeal be determine or withdraw . appeal : further provision 15 ( 1 ) if the Tribunal confirm or vary an account information notice or a penalty notice on an appeal under this Part , the person to whom the notice be give must comply with the notice — ( a ) within such period as may be specify by the Tribunal , or ( b ) if the Tribunal do not specify a period , within such period as may be specify by the Secretary of State and notify to the person . ( 2 ) a decision by the Tribunal on an appeal under this Part be final ( despite the provision of section 11 and 13 of the Tribunals , Courts and Enforcement Act 2007 ) . part 5 - General provision and interpretation relevant benefit 16 in this Schedule " relevant benefit " mean any of the following — ( a ) a relevant social security benefit as define in section 121DA ( 7 ) ; ( b ) a child tax credit or work tax credit under the Tax Credits Act 2002 ; ( c ) a payment , as mention in subsection ( 2 ) ( d ) of section 2 of the Employment and Training Act 1973 , under arrangement make under that section . account 17 in this schedule any reference to a person who hold an account include a reference to — ( a ) a person who hold an account jointly with one or more other person , and ( b ) a person who be a signatory , or one of the signatory , to an account , and " holder " be to be construe accordingly . general interpretation 18 in this schedule — " account " include a financial product ; ( 2 ) the power may be exercise only for the purpose of assist the Department in identify case which merit further consideration to establish whether relevant benefit be be pay or have be pay in accordance with the statutory provision and rule of law relate to those benefit . account information notice 2 ( 1 ) an account information notice be a notice require a person to give the Department — ( a ) the name of the holder of account that the person identify as be match account in relation to a specified relevant benefit , ( b ) other specify information relate to the holder of those account , and ( c ) such further information in connection with those account as may be specify . ( 3 ) a penalty notice give to a person must — ( a ) state the name and address of the person ; ( b ) give detail of the warning notice give to the person ; ( c ) state whether or not the Secretary of State have receive write representation in accordance with that notice ; ( d ) give reason for the Secretary of State ' s decision to impose a penalty on the person ; ( e ) state the amount of the penalty ; ( f ) give detail of how the penalty may be pay ; ( g ) specify the date before which the penalty must be pay ; ( h ) give detail about the person ' s right of appeal ; ( i ) give detail about the consequence of non - payment . ( 4 ) the date specify under sub - paragraph ( 3 ) ( g ) must be a date fall at least 28 day after the day on which the penalty notice be give . ( 5 ) the Secretary of State may cancel a penalty notice by give a notice to that effect to the person to whom the penalty notice be give . ( 6 ) if a penalty notice be cancel the Secretary of State — ( a ) may not give a further penalty notice in relation to the failure or conduct to which the notice relate , and ( b ) must repay any amount that have be pay in accordance with the notice . enforcement 4 if a person do not pay the whole or any part of a penalty which the person be liable to pay under this Schedule the penalty or part of the penalty be recoverable — ( a ) if the county court so order , as if it be payable under an order of that court ; ( b ) if the High Court so order , as if it be payable under an order of that court . appeal 5 ( 1 ) a person who be give a penalty notice may appeal to the first - tier Tribunal ( " the Tribunal " ) against the decision to give the notice or any requirement of it . ( 2 ) an appeal may be on the ground that the decision or requirement — ( a ) be base on an error of fact , ( b ) be wrong in law , or ( c ) be unreasonable . ( 3 ) but an appeal against the amount of a penalty may not be make on the ground mention in sub - paragraph ( 2 ) ( c ) . ( 4 ) an appeal under this paragraph must be make before the end of the period of 28 day begin with the day on which the penalty notice be give . ( 5 ) on an appeal the Tribunal may — ( a ) confirm or quash the decision to give the penalty notice , or ( b ) confirm or vary any requirement of it . ( 6 ) in determine an appeal the Tribunal may — ( a ) review any determination of fact on which the decision or requirement appeal against be base , and ( b ) take into account evidence which be not available to the Secretary of State when give the notice . ( 7 ) where an appeal in respect of a penalty notice be make under this paragraph the notice be of no effect until the appeal be determine or withdraw . ( 8 ) where an appeal be or may be make to the Upper Tribunal in relation to a decision of the Tribunal under this paragraph , the Upper Tribunal may suspend the notice to which the appeal relate until the appeal be determine or withdraw . ( 9 ) if the Tribunal confirm or vary a decision or requirement appeal against under this paragraph , the person to whom the penalty notice be give must comply with the notice or the notice as varied ( as the case may be ) — ( a ) within such period as may be specify by the Tribunal , or ( b ) if the Tribunal do not specify a period , within such period as may be specify by the Secretary of State and notify to the person .
