[ P002882 ] Refugee Family Reunion Routes : Sudan Motion make , and question propose , that this House do now adjourn . — ( Scott Mann . ) I be grateful to have the opportunity to draw the House ' s attention to the catastrophic situation in Sudan and to highlight the circumstance of the people in danger there , some of whom have family member recognise as refugee here in the United Kingdom . I hope to take this time to illustrate how the UK ' s family reunion rule make it incredibly difficult for those individual — most of they child — to join their family member here . finally , I want to ask the Government to think again about how they apply the family reunion rule , give the horrendous circumstance that those individual face , and to urge the Minister and his colleague to think about a new approach to facilitate and support reunion with family member here rather than hinder it , as seem to be the case in too many instance . I turn , first , to the circumstance in Sudan . what be unfold there have be describe by the United Nations as one of the " bad humanitarian nightmare in recent history . " since fighting break out between the sudanese armed force and the paramilitary Rapid Support Forces , more than 9 , 000 have be kill . horrific report of rape and sexual violence continue to emerge , and clash be increasingly along ethnic line , particularly in Darfur . every hour child be kill , injure or abduct . many hospital have have to suspend operation ; other have be bomb or turn into military basis . last month , the Minister for Africa say that the violence there bear " all the hallmark of ethnic cleansing " . the fighting that commence in mid - April have lead to more than 1 million people flee Sudan altogether to neighbour Chad , Egypt , Ethiopia , South Sudan and the Central African Republic . meanwhile , more than 5 million have be force from their home , internally displace within Sudan . among those displace be almost 1 . 5 million refugee and asylum seeker from other country , who have already have to flee persecution in their home territory to Sudan , particularly eritrean national . More than 6 million people be on the edge of famine , and more than 20 million face acute food insecurity . More than 4 million woman and girl face the risk of gender - base violence , with limited or no access to protection service and support . against that background , I have have the pleasure of work with the Refugee and Migrant Forum of Essex and London — RAMFEL — which have a number of refugee client here in the UK with family member stick in Sudan who want to get here . altogether , ramfel represent 14 individual — a tiny sample of that country — who have be struggle to leave Sudan to join their family here . seven month on from the start of the most recent conflict , only two have make it here so far . of those two , one — a child — be successful only after an appeal . of the 12 who have not yet make it here , all be child under 18 . ten be eritrean , and two be sudanese . of those 12 , eight be still in Sudan itself — child in a war zone , face extreme danger . the other four have make it to neighbouring country but , as we will see , they be not out of danger yet . to all reasonable observer , give the circumstance of those child , reunion with their family member in the United Kingdom must be appropriate and the right thing to do . be it not precisely for such situation that we have family reunion policy at all ? family reunion would provide a safe legal route to the UK , allow both the individual here and those come here to get on with rebuild their life . it would remove any temptation to seek assistance from people smuggler — break the business model , to borrow that expression . most fundamentally , those child would be safe . I commend the hon . member for Cumbernauld , Kilsyth and Kirkintilloch East ( Stuart C . McDonald ) on secure this debate — that constituency be quite a mouthful , and I hope I pronounce it right . he be at the fore in address this issue . in Sudan , 4 . 3 million people have be displace , and 1 . 1 million be live in five neighbouring country . the British Red Cross have be instrumental in reunite more than 10 , 000 displace people and their family . it can offer support with visa application if the individual be base in London , Liverpool , Preston or Plymouth , accord to its website . do he agree that it be important to have visa assistance hub throughout the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland , with at least one for the devolved institution in Northern Ireland . the hon . Gentleman make perfect sense . organisation such as the Red Cross and RAMFEL , which I have be work with on this topic , be fantastic . the more support we can give they and people across the United Kingdom , the well . these be precisely the circumstance in which we should have refugee family reunion rule . I regret to report that , unfortunately , the rule and process be make it hard for these people than it should be . in particular , while UK rule be pretty generous for spouse , partner and child — I acknowledge that — they be more restrictive for other category of relative , include sibling . Most of the child I be talk about today have lose their parent , and it be an old sibling here in the UK that they be seek to join . furthermore , the rule require enrolment of biometric information before an application will even be look at . that mean the child can not even get over the starting line , because the visa application centre in Sudan , understandably , have to close after the outbreak of the conflict . if there be no way to safely provide biometric information , surely we should stop ask for it in advance ? I will set out precisely how the application of the family reunion rule and procedure have impact on the child . I be use pseudonym to protect the identity of individual . sixteen - year - old Adila flee to Sudan to escape persecution in Eritrea , include force conscription into the army . as a lone 16 - year - old girl in a war zone , she clearly face significant risk . she have already be displace from Khartoum to a city in eastern Sudan and be struggle severely with her mental health . she seek family reunion with her old brother , who be a recognise refugee here in the UK . however , hers be one of a number of case that can not get off the ground because the Home Office insist she attend a visa application centre to enrol biometric information . the centre in Sudan be close , so that would mean have to make an irregular and dangerous journey to a neighbouring country to do it there . I acknowledge that the Home Office do consider application to defer enrolment of biometric information until the person either arrive at or be at least en route to the UK , so that the application can proceed . but even a cursory look at the relevant policy document show that it be only in very few circumstance indeed where the Home Office allow that to happen . when 16 - year - old Adila ask to defer enrolment , she be refuse that application . the Home Office say she have not prove her identity with reasonable certainty and assert that have cross one border irregularly — flee Eritrea to get to Sudan — she could obviously manage to do so again . I do not believe that that be a fair approach to take to a 16 - year - old girl in Sudan . Allowance have to be make for the fact that eritrean refugee in Sudan will almost certainly not be able to produce passport . a degree of latitude be therefore require . the idea that because someone flee over a border in fear of persecution , they can just be call on to make another dangerous and irregular journey be in itself a dangerous idea . it ride a coach and horse through the Home Office ' s own policy . it would not be worth the paper it be write on . if an unaccompanied 16 - year - old girl in a war zone can not avail herself of the deferral policy , who on earth can ? seven of the other individual be in a similar situation . they can not apply because they be in Sudan and there be no place to go to enrol their biometric information . even among those who have make it out of Sudan , similar issue can arise . for example , Fatima , a 15 - year - old eritrean girl , have originally make a family application to join her brother in the UK just prior to the outbreak of the war in Sudan . she have get as far as book an appointment at the visa application centre in Khartoum . that , of course , have to be cancel when the centre close after the outbreak of fighting . Fatima end up trafficked from Khartoum to South Sudan some week after the outbreak of war , and be release only on the payment of a ransom . she clearly remain at severe risk of kidnapping , sexual exploitation and all other manner of harm . there be no visa application centre in South Sudan , but again the Home Office refuse to defer biometric enrolment . ramfel ask the Home Office if , as an alternative , mobile biometric enrolment could take place — someone would travel to South Sudan from a regional VAC to take the biometric there . if require , RAMFEL would offer to pay , but even that reasonable offer be refuse . I ask the question again : if those circumstance do not merit the deferral of biometric enrolment or other compromise action , what on earth do ? be that not the problem with the hostile environment ? there be no circumstance ; they do not want people to come . it do not matter how dreadful the circumstance be that people be live in . it do not matter that this be the country where they have family member who can make they feel at home and welcome , and help they to start to overcome the trauma they have go through . the Home Office do not want to know . computer say no . the door be close . " computer say no " be pretty close to the bone . the Home Office have a policy on biometric enrolment , and it stick rigidly to it even when dramatic circumstance such as those persist in Sudan mean that a different approach should be take . the Home Office can take a different approach , and it have do so in certain circumstance . the Minister would not like it if I make a comparison with Ukraine , and I do not want to do so , but I simply point out that , in those incredible circumstance , the Home Office be able to take a different approach . I be not ask for anything remotely approach what be do in that situation ; I be just ask the Home Office to be a little more deft , a wee bit more responsive , and to think about the consideration that should apply for people apply from Sudan . I be sure my hon . friend be aware that there be a big sudanese community in Glasgow , and I remember a meeting I have with a number of sudanese people who make that very point about Ukraine . they say , " we want this country to look after Ukrainians . of course , it have to look after they ; they be go through a terrible war and they be be attack — but so be our family . what be the difference ? " do my hon . friend understand how important this debate will be to sudanese people live in this country ? at last , somebody be talk about their pain and care enough to secure a debate in the House of Commons . I know they really appreciate everything he be try to do . I be grateful to my hon . friend for her remark , but the tribute should be pay to RAMFEL and the other organisation out there that do amazing work on behalf of the sudanese community . there be people who would make a legitimate argument that there should be some sort of equivalence in the treatment of Ukraine and Sudan , but that be not the case I be make tonight . I be simply say that the Home Office show in the case of Ukraine that it be willing to apply different rule , or to apply the same rule differently . it be able to be nimble and to respond accordingly to a grave situation . this , too , be a grave situation and there should be some sort of flexibility in the response . on this point , the solution be pretty obvious : we need a more generous set of exception to the rule that require biometric information be provide in advance . I be not the only one say that . the House of Lords Justice and Home Affairs Committee recently report on family migration : " the Home Office should exercise its discretion to lift or delay the requirement to submit biometric when this would involve travel in dangerous condition or outside the applicant ' s country of residence . the Home Office should allow biometric to be complete on arrival in the UK for a wide range of nationality in crisis situation . " that seem to be the compassionate and common - sense thing to do . if the Minister be not willing to go as far as the Committee suggest , surely he must see that the application of the rule in the type of circumstance I have describe be gravely unsettling and must be revisit in some form . I turn next to rule in relation to sibling . even those who ultimately be able to jump through the first administrative hoop be far from guarantee success in their family reunion application . exist rule focus on family reunion for spouse and for child under 18 . I have speak in previous debate about various problem with what I regard as the overly restrictive category of relationship that can benefit from family reunion without further test apply , but today I will focus on sibling . give the situation prevail in Sudan and neighbouring country , many child find themselves either orphan or without any contact with their parent . for these kid , their sibling here in the UK be essentially their only remain family . that say , if a 15 - year - old seek to join their 20 - year - old brother here , they must first pay a fee and a health surcharge , unless they be grant a waiver , which add an additional hurdle . then , as well as prove their relationship , they must show that there be exceptional circumstance and that the refusal of their application would result in unjustifiably harsh consequence for the applicant . meet those test can be surprisingly difficult . it often seem that the general country situation , however hellish , will never be enough to make a person ' s circumstance — even a child ' s circumstance — exceptional enough to overcome that hurdle . a person seem to need to be able to show that their circumstance be exceptional , even compare with other individual in that country — in that warzone . that be a hugely difficult prospect , likely require legal advice and lawyer , and it be difficult to obtain the necessary evidence . surely the Home Office can be more responsive to the situation on the ground in Sudan . at the very least , could we not have clear guidance that any child live unaccompanie in Sudan should be treat as meet the necessary test of exceptionality and harsh consequence , and therefore should , in principle , be allow to be reunite with a UK - base sibling ? surely that be the bare minimum we can do . as I say , even if those test be overcome , the fact that sibling be not consider " core " family member for the purpose of the rule have other consequence . I turn to another case study . two unaccompanied eritrean child see a household member kill . one of the kid be beat up during the same raid . they submit application for family reunion in November 2022 , some month before the most recent upsurge in fighting . the application be originally refuse , but an appeal be lodge and the Home Office eventually concede it . that be welcome , but the Home Office be now insist on payment of the immigration health surcharge , which , of course , the family simply can not afford . surely in such circumstance any fee or health surcharge should be waive . finally , I turn to processing time . if one of these kid be somehow in a position to jump through all the hoop I have describe , surely the least we will offer be a speedy priority service . the service standard for family reunion application be 12 week , but I be tell that many application take six month to a year . if an appeal be require in order to overturn a refusal — we have just hear about an example of that — the wait can be more than double . family separation will always be painful , but for unaccompanied child in Sudan , and even in some of the neighbouring country , it be also seriously dangerous . surely some sort of priority processing have to be give to case where the applicant be directly in danger . another case study involve Wissam , who be 17 , and Abdul , who be 14 . they apply to join their old brother just before war break out and have an appointment to enrol their biometric in Khartoum . that could not happen , as the centre close down . struggle to access food and water , and at risk of kidnapping , trafficking or exploitation , the brother be victim of robbery . ultimately , they decide to flee again and make a dangerous , irregular journey to Uganda . they now live unaccompanie in cramp condition and , because of their age and nationality , face regular discrimination in access sanitation , include clean water . the 14 - year - old be struggle with mental health issue and suffering night terror because of his experience in Sudan and on the journey to Uganda . surely we can not leave those two brother , who be now in a position to submit their application , to wait for month and perhaps year . surely application have to be give priority in those circumstance . the Minister will no doubt tell we about the significant number of people who do arrive here in the UK under our family reunion arrangement . I acknowledge that fact and I welcome it . however , it would be totally wrong to say that the system be function well ; various report by the independent chief inspector of border and immigration testify to that . lot of improvement still have to be make . I be not ask for a revolution today , although perhaps I will pursue that far in the month to come . today , I simply ask that the Home Office accept that it have to be nimble , to respond and to tweak its rule and process where circumstance require . the utterly dire circumstance in Sudan surely justify such a response . in summary , I be ask the Home Office three thing . first , I ask it to rethink the requirement for people trap in Sudan — particularly child — to provide biometric in advance at a visa application centre . please look at alternative , whether wait until people ' s arrival in the UK before require biometric , or some other compromise that do not hold up the consideration of application . secondly , I ask the Home Office , either by tweak the rule or , perhaps more realistically , by issue guidance for case such as those I have describe , to make it clear that , as a general rule , child from Sudan seek to join sibling or other family member in the UK should be treat as meet the " exceptional " test for the family reunion rule . I would like to think that that would be apply to sibling more generally , but for today ' s purpose I make a special case for those seek to leave Sudan . I also ask the Home Office not to make any such application subject to fee and health surcharge . thirdly , I ask the Home Office to prioritise these application , in recognition of the danger that the people make they face . do not leave they wait for month . finally , if possible , seek to work with international organisation and non - governmental organisation to help support safe passage from Sudan , as and when application be allow . I close with a warning , because the danger be that if we do not facilitate their application , these youngster will end up seek to make their own way to the UK , irregularly and dangerously . that bring I to the final case I want to mention , which be that of 16 - year - old Daoud , who flee Eritrea to Sudan . in the light of the situation there , he flee again , to South Sudan . with no progress on secure refugee family reunion from there , he take matter into his own hand and start make his way towards the Mediterranean . he be currently arbitrarily detain in Libya . some might say he make his own choice , but I think we leave he with no choice at all . I do not want to have to come back here in a few month with another Adjournment debate on this subject and to have to provide similar — or even bad — update on the other child I have mention in this debate . I know the Minister can not make policy on the hoof , but I urge he to speak with official , to rethink the Home Office strategy in relation to those who be suffer in Sudan , and to ensure that we be do all we can to facilitate and support family reunion . I thank the hon . member for Cumbernauld , Kilsyth and Kirkintilloch East ( Stuart C . mcdonald ) for secure this Adjournment debate . we share his deep concern about the situation in Sudan and all those affect by it , include those seek refugee status in the United Kingdom or other safe country . the Government remain committed to uphold the principle of family reunion by provide a safe and legal route to bring family together through the refugee family reunion policy . the family reunion route allow individual with protection status in the UK to sponsor their partner or child to stay with or join they here , provide they form part of a family unit before the sponsor flee their country of origin to seek protection . while we sympathise greatly with the situation in which many individual in Sudan find themselves , we do not intend to prioritise refugee family reunion application from those impact by the sudanese conflict , as there be many other individual in the queue who will be face broadly comparable situation elsewhere in the world . we want to treat all individual face such situation in the same manner and ensure that , where appropriate , they can be support to a life in the UK in accordance with our rule . I would not necessarily say that people seek to come here from Sudan because they be in danger there should be prioritise ahead of other who face similar risk elsewhere — a point that the Minister fairly make — but do the Home Office make any consideration or assessment of risk at all ? there be people who apply for refugee family reunion , quite rightly and fairly , who do not face any imminent risk because they be in a relatively safe third country . surely the fact that people be face real danger be an add reason to give priority to their family reunion application . that should be something that the Department consider . the hon . Gentleman make a valid point , which I be happy to take up with my official . our policy be one of non - discrimination , so individual be treat equally , regardless of their country of origin . obviously , there be a number of place in the world with great danger and we do not choose to rank they in order of priority . however , I can see some merit in what he be say , so I be happy to give that consideration . it be important to note that the UK have a very strong record of support refugee . since 2015 , we have resettle over half a million people seek safety , which be among the most generous offering in our country ' s history . the UK rank highly among other develop country in that regard . we continue to welcome refugee through our exist global resettlement scheme , include the UK resettlement scheme itself , community sponsorship and the mandate resettlement scheme . since 2015 , we have issue 49 , 000 family reunion visa to family member of those with protection status , with over half of those visa for child . that figure demonstrate our commitment to refugee family reunion . we have welcome sudanese national through both our UK resettlement scheme and the community sponsorship scheme in 2022 and 2023 . between 2015 and 2023 , 6 , 500 sudanese national have be grant visa under refugee family reunion . in the year to September 2023 , 618 sudanese national be grant visa under refugee family reunion . the UK be make a significant commitment , although of course the need be very great , as the hon . Gentleman say , due to the situation in Sudan . we will continue to consider our approach to refugee family reunion in the round rather than on a crisis - by - crisis basis . the UK have no plan at the moment to introduce a designate resettlement scheme for sudanese refugee . as a general rule , it be important that the UK do not treat migration as the first lever that we pull to try to help people in grave situation in the world . generally speak , the great impact that the UK can make , whether that be in Sudan or in other crisis situation , be by use our full diplomatic muscle and our development aid to support people in the region , which be , in fact , the place where the majority of refugee find themselves . indeed , that happen with respect to the sudanese situation , where hundred of thousand of individual be be support by the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees and other organisation in the immediate environ of Sudan . the UK be proud to be support those effort to help those individual . I wish to turn more specifically to some of the very valid question that the hon . Gentleman raise . first , he raise the question of those flee conflict zone who find it difficult to provide document for family reunion purpose . we recognise that this be a challenge for those flee their home and their home country . although the onus be on the applicant to show that the relationship be genuine , there be no specific requirement to provide certain type of evidence . we recognise that documentary evidence may not always be available , particularly in country where there be no function administrative authority to issue a passport , a marriage certificate , or a birth certificate . decision maker should take into consideration evidence from a range of source , include information provide by their UK family sponsor . each decision be consider on the balance of probability to identify whether there be sufficient evidence to prove that the individual be relate as claim . it be important to prevent abuse of the refugee family reunion policy and to safeguard applicant by carefully review their application where fraudulent document be submit , or where there be evidence that the sponsor obtain leave by deception . with more specific regard to the situation in Sudan , the hon . Gentleman be right to say that the visa application centre in Khartoum be close until further notice . as a result , any passport remain there be have to be hold in secure storage . we be committed to do everything we can to support people who find themselves affect by that closure and to reopen the centre as soon as it be safe to do so for our staff and their contractor . there be other visa application centre in the wide vicinity of Sudan . I appreciate that the distance be long , and that the journey can be arduous and , at time , unsafe . we do have visa centre in Cairo and Jeddah , and many people have make use of those in the time since the crisis begin . even among the case that I speak about , one or two individual have make it into a neighbouring country — unfortunately one have make it to South Sudan where there be also not a visa application centre — but surely , particularly in the case of child , it be too much to ask they to make a dangerous journey such as that to supply biometric information . there should be some sort of presumption against the need to provide biometric information , or at least a willingness to consider defer it before the Home Office even look at the application . in most case , unfortunately , individual will have to make a journey to leave Sudan , as it be very unlikely that they will fly directly from Sudan . Most of the case that I have be make aware of as Immigration Minister be of individual who have make the journey to Cairo or to Jeddah or other neighbouring country . rise — before I give way to the hon . Gentleman , I will reply directly on the biometric point , which be an important question . fundamentally , we believe that biometric be extremely important , because we want to protect the UK ' s national security and the safety of our citizen here . although , of course , we all want to see the good in individual come here , particularly in young people and child , there be individual whom we would not want to enter the United Kingdom . as such , biometric , in the form of facial image and fingerprint , underpin our immigration system . however , we make exception for individual who find themselves in the most difficult situation . we publish guidance in May 2023 , which set out our approach to handle applicant who claim that it be unsafe to travel from Sudan to a visa application centre in another country to enrol their biometric — he refer to that situation in his speech . the guidance set out the circumstance under which UK Visas and Immigration will either predetermine an application or defer the requirement to enrol biometric information until the applicant arrive in the UK , when the applicant have demonstrate their circumstance to be exceptional . in most case , we require biometric to be take as part of the application so that we can conduct the check on a person ' s identity and suitability to come to the UK . it be ultimately the responsibility of the applicant to satisfy the decision maker about their identity . I hope that the hon . Gentleman can take some comfort from the fact that the guidance give that flexibility . I hear that he feel that it be be apply too onerously and in a way that be insufficiently sensitive to the situation in Sudan . I be happy to take that away , speak to my official and , if he have further example , to put those in front of they so that we can make sure that the guidance be be apply fairly . I be grateful that the Minister be open to have a discussion about this issue . he be right that , ultimately , all these kid will probably have to leave for a neighbouring country for onward travel . however , it be one thing to ask they to leave in the certainty that they will be allow into the United Kingdom ; it be another to ask they to leave and provide biometric information on the off - chance that they might be allow in at some future point . one compromise might be to consider the family reunion application without the biometric information ; if it be grant , then tell they to come to a neighbouring country and provide the biometric information there . will the Minister take that away and think about it ? I will be happy to look into that and come back to the hon . gentleman . we both agree that biometric be important . we want to ensure that they be compromise only in the most exceptional circumstance so that we can protect national security , but it be important that we show a degree of discretion when people — young people , in particular — find themselves in the hard of situation . I will be happy to look into the issue and write to he . the hon . Gentleman also mention processing time for family reunion application , and I want to address that directly . in general , UKVI be operate well and be meet its service standard in all , or almost all , visa category , but there be delay with respect to family reunion — a point that he and other member have raise in the past . we acknowledge the need to dedicate more resource to support the safe and legal route and be review process to streamline decision making to make it more efficient for applicant . we recognise that the family member of those with protection status in the UK be particularly vulnerable . when the out - of - country decision make team receive a request for prioritisation from an applicant or their representative , that will be assess to determine whether the application should be prioritise . as I say in answer to the hon . Gentleman ' s previous comment , we do not prioritise in a blanket way because of nationality , but we do give priority to case involve particularly vulnerable individual . example of ground for prioritisation may include applicant or sponsor who have serious medical condition or terminal illness . the list of ground for prioritisation be non - exhaustive ; manager undertake a holistic consideration of the applicant ' s circumstance when consider a request for prioritisation . the hon . Gentleman also ask about the cost of refugee family reunion . it be free — no fee it levy , although he do raise some of the ally cost that go with it . we make sure that the route be free for obvious reason . the hon . Gentleman also ask about child sponsor . the family reunion policy be intend to allow those grant protection status in the UK to sponsor , pre - flight , immediate family member to join they here . we must avoid create an incentive for people , particularly child , to leave their family and risk very dangerous journey , hope that relative will be able to join they later . we do , unfortunately , come across example of that , include through the small boat route , which be among the most perilous of journey that a child could make . there be other provision in the immigration rule that cater for extended family member and , where a valid application do not meet the criterion within our rule , include child sponsor , we consider whether there be compelling compassionate factor that warrant a granting outside the rule . we believe that be child allow to sponsor parent , that would create a real risk of an incentive for more child to be encourage , or even force , to leave their family and risk very hazardous journey to the UK . that play into the hand of criminal gang that exploit vulnerable people , and go against all our safeguard responsibility and instinct . our policy be not design to keep child refugee apart from their parent , but in consider any policy we have to think carefully about the wide impact to avoid put more people unnecessarily into harm ' s way . finally , I will answer the broad question about refugee resettlement . we have a proud record as a country , have offer half a million people a safe and legal route into the UK . we understand that the scale of disruption and situation around the world mean that so many people find themselves in grave need . our approach have to be consider very carefully , but we want to continue to work with international organisation , such as the one that the hon . member reference . we have a good relationship with the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees through our global resettlement scheme , and early in the year , through the Illegal Migration Act 2023 , we legislate so that we can introduce further scheme in the future . I recently launch a consultation in which we ask every local authority in the whole of the United Kingdom to give we their capacity to take refugee on such scheme over the course of the year to come . that consultation be open and I encourage the hon . member to talk to his local authority and see whether it be take part in it . we will carefully consider the response , and if they suggest that there be further capacity across the UK , that will lead we either to extend exist scheme or to create new one so that the UK can play an even great and more generous role in the year ahead in help more people from place such as Sudan to come to the UK . I thank the hon . member for secure the debate , and all our colleague tonight who have listen or contribute . I fully understand the interest in the subject , give the great concern that everyone feel about the situation in Sudan . I hope that I have set out our record and the work that we be do , and give he some assurance that he and I can work closely together to learn from his experience , and his evident sincere concern about the issue , to ensure that the scheme be operate as well as it can . question put and agree to .
